How engagement is detected

A reply is classified as engaging with gardener if it matches one or more signals:

  • mentions-gardener — mentions "gardener", "repo-gardener", "context tree", etc.
  • references-verdict — references verdict terms (ALIGNED, NEEDS_REVIEW, severity, etc.)
  • quotes-gardener — markdown blockquote containing gardener text
  • addresses-review — phrases like "addressed findings", "response to gardener", "update pushed"

🌱 gardener · NEW_TERRITORY · severity: low · commit: aa967986

> What is this? repo-gardener checks whether PRs and issues fit the project's product decisions, architecture, and roadmap — not code correctness. Think of it as a product-context review layer. For code review, see Greptile/CodeRabbit.

### Context fit

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | This PR | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|---------|---------------|-----|
| Mobile onboarding | Fixes permissions and signup handoff for mobile web handoff routes | No tree guidance on mobile client support or onboarding handoff flows | 🆕 New |
| Auth routes | Adjusts auth page behavior for mobile signup flow | Auth modes documented (local_trusted vs authenticated) but mobile-specific auth not covered | 🆕 New |
| Agent/company routes | Adds permission adjustments for mobile context | Route/service split pattern followed (engineering/backend/NODE.md) | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — Route/service split architecture
- [infrastructure/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/infrastructure/NODE.md) — Two deployment modes (local_trusted vs authenticated)
- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — Local-first, cloud-ready (decision #8)

</details>

### Recommendation

Why: Mobile client support is a new surface area not yet documented in the context tree. This is the second PR in this series (follows #3594) establishing mobile onboarding as an ongoing effort.

Suggested path forward: If mobile becomes a sustained effort, consider adding a tree node under product/ or engineering/frontend/ documenting mobile support scope and constraints. Low risk as-is — the code changes follow existing patterns.

PR #3302 Fix plugin page routes doubling company prefix on company switch
ALIGNED low open PENDING by @harperaa · 2026-04-10T13:25:04Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: 6363ab3b

Aligned with context tree. No concerns.

Direct fix for issue #3264 by the same reporter (@harperaa) who filed it — nice closing of the loop. The change matches the proposed fix exactly: instead of enumerating board routes and stripping only those, the new logic strips the company prefix whenever the first segment is not a global or board route. That's the right inversion — it treats plugin page routes as first-class citizens of the routing layer without requiring every new plugin to register itself in a central enumeration, which aligns with the tree's "thin core, rich edges" stance toward plugins.

The regression tests are well-structured: three separate test cases covering plugin page routes (the bug), board routes (to prove the fix doesn't regress existing behavior), and global routes (to prove the fix doesn't over-strip). The docstring explicitly links back to issue #3264, which makes the test self-documenting for future readers.

Two-line code change, 24-line test file. Perfect scope. Once this lands, issue #3264 can be closed.

Issue #3301 [BUG] OpenCode: Non-interactive mode fails on "Read before Write" guardrail instead of self-correcting
ALIGNED medium open by @MSandro · 2026-04-10T13:05:33Z → gardener comment 1 other

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: medium · issue snapshot: 2026-04-10T12:58Z

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Clear, well-diagnosed bug. Aligns with an existing class of "tool errors treated as terminal failures" bugs in the opencode-local adapter, and the tree's "surface problems, don't hide them" principle gives a clean framing for the fix. This is the same root cause as #3193 — worth linking so a single fix addresses both symptoms.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Tool-error vs run-error classification | Keep guardrail/tool errors in the agent's thought chain, not bubble as terminal failure | "Surface problems, don't hide them" — silent termination on recoverable errors is the anti-pattern | ✅ Aligned |
| Adapter-owned error shaping | Fix belongs in opencode-local JSONL parser / lifecycle code | Adapters parse agent output into the shared TranscriptEntry types | ✅ Aligned |
| Control plane boundary | Paperclip surfaces exit code; adapter decides what's terminal | "Adapters do NOT own task scheduling" but DO own "parsing agent output" | ✅ Aligned |
| Self-correction loop | Agent learns from adapter error and retries within the same run | Autonomous tasks must be able to recover from recoverable errors | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [adapters/opencode-local/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/opencode-local/NODE.md) — adapter lifecycle and output parsing contract
- [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md) — adapter abstraction, three-layer package structure, session management
- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — "Surface problems, don't hide them"
- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — task communication and recovery semantics

</details>

### Duplicate root cause

Issue #3193 ("opencode_local treats tool_use errors as terminal adapter failures") reports the same class of bug from a different angle: tool-level errors in the OpenCode JSONL stream are being folded into the same terminal-error signal as run-level failures. This issue (#3301) is the user-facing symptom of that same misclassification, specifically for the "Read before Write" guardrail. A single fix to the JSONL parser in packages/adapters/opencode-local/src/server/parse.ts (or equivalent) should address both.

Worth linking the two issues and treating them as one work item.

### Recommendation — solution ranking

The reporter proposes three solutions. Ranking them by tree alignment and blast radius:

1. Fix the JSONL parser first (implied by #3193 but not yet done). This is the root-cause fix: tool errors stay in the transcript, only fatal adapter errors bubble up as run-level failures. Scoped to the adapter package, no cross-domain changes. Do this regardless of the other options.

2. OpenCode server API transition (reporter's option 1) is architecturally attractive but much larger scope — it would enable persistent sessions and finer-grained error recovery, but deserves a dedicated design discussion and tree node under adapters/opencode-local/ describing the lifecycle shift. Not a prerequisite for fixing this bug.

3. Retry-loop logic in Paperclip (reporter's option 2) should be avoided — it crosses the adapter boundary. Paperclip's control plane shouldn't know about "adapter_failed" strings or special-case opencode error patterns; that's the adapter's job to classify correctly.

4. --session/--continue flags (reporter's option 3) is a useful supplement to option 1, but only after the parser is fixed. If the parser still classifies tool errors as terminal, CLI-level session persistence doesn't help.

### Related tree observations

This is now the fifth or sixth instance of the "something silently fails instead of being recoverable" pattern I've flagged across recent PRs and issues in this gardener run (#3282, #3215, #3207, #3284, #3290, and now #3301/#3193). Worth considering whether adapters/NODE.md should grow a short section on error classification conventions — specifically "tool errors vs adapter errors vs run errors" — so future adapter authors have a clear rule to follow. The current split looks like each adapter invents its own boundary.

---

ahosker · 2026-04-11T21:10:53Z

It would be best to link to the opencode server rather than use the CLI, as that is where the development is headed.
I presume it would also reduce server resources, as each agent would hook into the existing server rather than create its own.

However, this was causing me real pain.

## Temporary solution
opencode already has a built-in bypass: set OPENCODE_DISABLE_FILETIME_CHECK=true before starting the CLI.
Example:
OPENCODE_DISABLE_FILETIME_CHECK=true opencode
Or export it in your shell:
export OPENCODE_DISABLE_FILETIME_CHECK=true

What it does:
- Disables the "read before overwrite" check
- Also disables the "file changed since last read" protection

Where it lives:
- packages/opencode/src/file/time.ts:90
- packages/opencode/src/flag/flag.ts:73

## How To in Paperclip
In each agent, you can set OpenCode Environment Variables.

PR #3300 fix(server): re-read index.html per request to fix black page on direct URL navigation
NEEDS_REVIEW high open PENDING by @anhermon · 2026-04-10T12:45:59Z → gardener comment 1 engaging
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: high · commit: 4ce3604e

> [!WARNING]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. This review flags a scoping issue that should be addressed before any part of this PR lands.

### Summary

The stated fix is legit — re-reading index.html per request instead of caching at startup closes a real black-page bug on SPA direct navigation after a UI rebuild. But this PR is not a small fix. It is a 74-commit, 147-file, 12,834-addition bundle that spans months of fork-internal work: adapter failure taxonomy, heartbeat/memory gates, Telegram integration, self-hosted OpenTelemetry stack, remote_trigger adapter, agent bundles (cowork/agents/*), new plugin examples, workflows, and more. The stated fix is ~0.1% of the actual diff.

This is almost certainly a mistaken branch target. The branch name is fix/anga-766-spa-routing-stale-index-html but it contains commits from dozens of unrelated ANGA-* tickets. Either the author meant to open a branch with only the ANGA-766 commits, or the fork branch was never rebased onto a clean base for the upstream PR.

### Concerns

1. Impossible to review as one PR. 74 commits across adapter, heartbeat, plugins, observability, telegram, agent bundles, and workflows is far beyond what any reviewer can sanely evaluate in one sitting. Even if every change is individually correct, they should be reviewed independently.

2. Potential fork-internal content leak. The diff includes cowork/agents/{brand-artist,career-monitor,cto,dev-agent-platform,dev-agent-products,learning-agent-2,operations-lead,visibility-agent,youtube-ingest}/ instruction bundles, Taskfile additions, doc/AGENT-GIT-WORKFLOW.md, doc/PUSH_CONVENTION.md, and a plan doc at docs/plans/2026-04-01-claude-rate-limit-fallback-investigation.md. Some of that looks like org-internal material (agent personas, internal workflow docs) that the author may not intend to open-source. Worth double-checking before any of this lands.

3. Possibly conflicting changes with in-flight PRs. This branch touches several files that are currently under review in other PRs:
- packages/adapters/claude-local/src/server/execute.ts and parse.ts — also touched by PRs #3296, #3297, #3299
- packages/adapter-utils/src/types.ts — also touched by #3296, #3297
- packages/adapters/codex-local/src/server/execute.ts — also touched by #3298
- packages/adapters/gemini-local/src/server/execute.ts — conflicts with ongoing gemini work

Landing this as-is would create hard-to-resolve merge conflicts for multiple open PRs.

4. Scope laundering risk. A PR whose title claims a 9-line fix but contains 12k lines of unrelated changes defeats the "small, reviewable PRs" model and the governance principle that every change should be independently auditable. This is the exact inverse of the scoping discipline we just saw on PR #3294 → PR #3296/#3297 (which split one bundled fix into two focused PRs).

### Recommendation

Before any part of this lands:

1. Close this PR and open a small, focused one for the ANGA-766 fix (re-read index.html per request + the matching test). That fix is legitimate and should land on its own — estimated size: 1 file, ~10 lines, plus a regression test.

2. If the author wants to contribute the other changes upstream, open separate PRs per logical unit:
- Adapter failure taxonomy + fallback chain (ANGA-184/205) — one PR
- Self-hosted OpenTelemetry observability stack — one PR (large, but architecturally distinct)
- remote_trigger adapter type — one PR
- Memory pre-flight gate (ANGA-165) — one PR, and coordinate with PR #3250 / #3289 (two active memory PRs)
- Telegram integration — one PR (note: this may conflict with "Thin core, rich edges" tree guidance — telegram is likely plugin territory)

3. Audit the diff for fork-internal content before re-opening. Agent bundles under cowork/agents/ and internal workflow docs may not be intended for upstream.

### Scope laundering note for gardener runbook

Gardener should probably flag any PR whose diff size is dramatically larger than what the title suggests, regardless of alignment, because scope laundering is itself a governance concern. This PR is the clearest example I've seen — stated as a 9-line SPA routing fix, delivered as 12,834 lines across 74 commits.

PR #3299 [codex] Clarify Claude instruction sibling file base path
ALIGNED low closed CORRECT by @aronprins · 2026-04-10T12:35:06Z → gardener comment 1 engaging 2 other

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: 724893ad

Aligned with context tree. No concerns.

Minimal, well-scoped fix. Claude adapter's instruction wrapper now explicitly treats the instructionsFileDir as the authoritative base for sibling files like ./HEARTBEAT.md, ./SOUL.md, ./TOOLS.md — closes an onboarding-time failure where fresh CEO agents tried to read siblings from the parent agent directory instead of the managed bundle directory. This is exactly the kind of adapter-owned path semantics the tree expects to live inside the adapter package, and the regression test asserts the stronger directive during the resume-to-fresh fallback path. No cross-domain impact, no bundle persistence change. Related to prior issue #3191 which flagged a similar "sibling file resolution" class of bug in the managed AGENTS.md bundle — worth the reviewer confirming both paths now resolve consistently.

PR #3298 [codex] add codex local login flow
ALIGNED low open PENDING by @roselloagents · 2026-04-10T12:25:57Z → gardener comment

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: b3c10821

Aligned with context tree. No concerns.

Clean adapter feature. Mirrors the existing Claude login recovery flow exactly, which is the right precedent — Paperclip control plane exposes a UI action, the adapter owns the CLI invocation using its managed CODEX_HOME strategy, and the codex_auth_required error code lets the UI react when auth is missing mid-run. - Adapter abstraction: authentication lifecycle lives in the adapter, not in core orchestration

One small note: the PR description mentions pnpm build still fails on Windows because the repo build script uses cp -r. That's unrelated to this PR and worth a separate issue so it doesn't block Windows contributors.

<details open><summary><h3>Security Review</h3></summary>

- Plain-text token storage (ui/src/adapters/openclaw-gateway/config-fields.tsx, packages/adapters/openclaw-gateway/src/ui/build-config.ts): x-openclaw-token is written directly into adapterConfig.headers as plain JSON in the agent record. It is not passed through normalizeAdapterConfigForPersistence and therefore bypasses the secrets vault. The value is visible in any API response or DB backup that returns the agent config. This is a deliberately broad surface by design; operators are warned at startup and can tighten it via extraArgs.

This is a comment left during a code review.
Path: packages/adapters/claude-local/src/server/parse.ts
Line: 183-186

Comment:
Raw stdout scan can false-positive on assistant text

The first branch tests the entire raw stdout string for phrases like "hit your limit" and "you've hit your limit". Because stdout is stream-JSON, an assistant turn whose text content happens to contain those words (e.g., a model response about API quotas) would trigger a false-rate-limit classification and suppress the claude_hello_probe_passed / _unexpected_output check. The safer approach is to restrict this scan to lines whose type is rate_limit_event or result, rather than matching the full stdout payload:

ts
// Instead of testing the raw stdout blob, only flag specific stream-JSON event types:
const hasRateLimitEvent = stdout.split(/\r?\n/).some((line) => {
  try {
    const ev = JSON.parse(line.trim());
    return ev?.type === "rate_limit_event" || ev?.error === "rate_limit";
  } catch { return false; }
});
if (hasRateLimitEvent) return true;

How can I resolve this? If you propose a fix, please make it concise.

PR #3295 Troubleshooting dangerouslySkipPermissions configuration issue
ALIGNED low open PENDING by @glide-the · 2026-04-10T12:15:57Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: fdecac8e

Aligned with context tree. No concerns that block merge, but a few worth noting for reviewers.

The core change is a clean single-source-of-truth refactor: three UI codepaths (NewAgent, OnboardingWizard, AgentConfigForm) each carried their own inline per-adapter default dictionaries, which had drifted. Extracting adapterConfigDefaults + getCreateValuesForAdapterType() eliminates the drift. Server-side normalization in applyAdapterConfigDefaults is actually MORE correct than UI-side defaults alone — API callers (CLI, scripts, plugins) now get the default too, not just users creating via the web UI. Good instinct.

### Notes for reviewers

1. PR scope is broader than the description suggests. The PR body says "UI-only default logic" and "no server, or adapter runtime changes" but the diff includes:
- Server-side normalization in server/src/routes/agents.ts (applyAdapterConfigDefaults now writes a dangerouslySkipPermissions default for claude_local and opencode_local)
- A behavior change to asBoolean in packages/adapter-utils/src/server-utils.ts (now accepts string "true"/"false" case-insensitively, was boolean-only)
- A new 314-line dangerously-skip-permissions.test.ts

Both extra changes are safe and well-tested, but the "low risk, UI-only" framing is misleading. Worth updating the PR description so CODEOWNERS/reviewers see the full scope.

2. Interaction with PR #3294 (still open). PR #3294 introduces resolveDangerouslySkipPermissions() in the claude-local adapter that overrides the configured value to false when Paperclip runs as root. If both PRs land, the data flow becomes:
- UI writes dangerouslySkipPermissions: true from the shared default
- Server normalizes to true if missing (this PR)
- Adapter overrides to false at execute time on root (#3294)

The config stored in the DB says one thing; the runtime does another. That's not a bug per se, but it creates a surprising diagnostic experience — operators will see dangerouslySkipPermissions: true in agent config but no --dangerously-skip-permissions flag in the transcript. Worth coordinating with #3294 or adding a logger.info explaining the override when it fires.

3. asBoolean widening is a cross-cutting behavior change. The new string coercion ("true" → true, "false" → false, case-insensitive) affects every caller of asBoolean across the codebase. The widening is backwards-compatible (existing boolean inputs behave identically), and the coercion only fires on string inputs that previously fell through to the fallback. The test coverage is thorough. Low risk, but worth calling out because adapter-utils contract changes are the kind of thing that can surprise plugin authors or downstream adapters — the utility's signature lives in @paperclipai/adapter-utils which is part of the stable surface.

4. dangerouslySkipPermissions: true as the default is a load-bearing security decision. The inline comment explains it correctly (headless mode has no interactive prompts), but it's worth documenting in the context tree under adapters/ as an explicit policy so future adapter authors know the rationale and don't re-litigate it.

### Recommendation

Land it. The refactor is good, the server-side enforcement is the right layer, and the tests are solid. Just (a) update the PR description to reflect the full scope, (b) add a coordination note to PR #3294 about the config-vs-runtime override interaction, and (c) consider adding a one-paragraph note to adapters/NODE.md or the tree about the "headless mode default skip" policy so the rationale is discoverable.

PR #3294 fix: OpenClaw gateway schema, Claude probe rate limits, UI token + embedded PG root
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open PENDING by @htsago · 2026-04-10T12:06:00Z → gardener comment 1 other
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · commit: 5ba2663a

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

The individual fixes are all technically reasonable and several align well with the tree. Two product-fit concerns deserve a maintainer call: (1) the PR bundles four logically distinct fixes, which makes review and bisect harder; (2) several of the changes implicitly expand "running Paperclip as root" into a supported deployment mode, which contradicts what infrastructure/deployment/NODE.md documents.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match per sub-fix</strong></summary>

| Sub-fix | Tree guidance | Fit |
|---------|---------------|-----|
| OpenClaw context → extraSystemPrompt | Adapter owns agent-param shaping | ✅ Aligned |
| OpenClaw token via env var / _FILE | Secrets are provider-abstracted, *_FILE matches Docker/K8s pattern | ✅ Aligned |
| Claude rate-limit reclassification | "Surface problems, don't hide them" — classifies but doesn't hide | ✅ Aligned |
| Claude root-UID auto-disable --dangerously-skip-permissions | Adapter knows its CLI constraints | ✅ Aligned |
| CLAUDE_ROOT_HEADLESS_ALLOWED_TOOLS hardcoded allowlist including Bash(*) | Governance-first / least privilege | ❓ Partial |
| Embedded PG createPostgresUser: true when uid=0 | infrastructure/deployment documents UID/GID remapping, not running as root | ❓ Conflict |
| Implicit expansion of "run as root" deployment mode | "UID/GID remapping for volume permissions" pattern already exists | ❓ Partial |
| UI gateway token field in CreateConfigValues | Secrets should flow through secretService.normalizeAdapterConfigForPersistence | ❓ Unclear |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [infrastructure/deployment/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/infrastructure/deployment/NODE.md) — "UID/GID remapping for volume permissions" — the docker entrypoint remaps the node user and gosus to it, which means Paperclip should not run as uid 0 in production
- [adapters/claude-local/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/claude-local/NODE.md) — Claude adapter owns CLI invocation and flag resolution
- [adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md) — OpenClaw gateway transport and context shaping
- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — Secrets are provider-abstracted

</details>

### Questions for maintainers

1. Should this be split into two or three PRs? The four sub-fixes are:
- OpenClaw schema + token resolution (adapter concern)
- Claude rate-limit reclassification (adapter concern)
- Root-UID handling across claude-local + embedded-PG (deployment concern)
- UI gateway token field (frontend concern)

Landing as one bundle makes the "run as root" story hard to discuss independently from the OpenClaw fix. Splitting lets each get a focused review and makes bisect/revert cleaner.

2. Is "run Paperclip as root" now a supported mode? The infrastructure/deployment tree node documents that the Docker entrypoint uses gosu to drop to the node user specifically to avoid running as root. This PR adds code paths that only fire when Paperclip runs as root:
- createPostgresUser: true for embedded-postgres
- Auto-disable --dangerously-skip-permissions for Claude CLI
- Inject --allowed-tools default allowlist

These fixes only make sense if "run as root" is a deliberately supported mode. If so, the deployment tree node should be updated to describe the two modes (gosu-remapped vs. root-direct) and when each is appropriate. If not, the fixes may be protecting a misconfiguration that operators should be correcting upstream (e.g., by setting USER_UID/USER_GID correctly).

3. Is the CLAUDE_ROOT_HEADLESS_ALLOWED_TOOLS list tight enough? The comment in the code frames this as "safer than --dangerously-skip-permissions", but Bash(*) is effectively unrestricted shell access, and the list also includes Write, Edit, WebFetch, Task, RemoteTrigger, EnterWorktree. That's the same blast radius as --dangerously-skip-permissions, just expressed differently. Two alternatives worth considering:
- Keep the hardcoded default but add a logger.warn at startup explaining "Paperclip is running as root; Claude is configured with a broad tool allowlist. Run as a non-root user for finer-grained permission control."
- Make the allowlist configurable per deployment via env var or adapter config so operators can tighten it without patching the code.

4. UI gateway token field — confirm that CreateConfigValues.openclawGatewayToken flows through secretService.normalizeAdapterConfigForPersistence and is stored in the vault, not in plain JSON in agent.adapterConfig. The PR description mentions adding the field but not the secret-handling path.

### Recommendation

Don't block on the core direction — the individual fixes address real bugs. But before merge:

- Split the PR into an OpenClaw/Claude adapter fixes PR and a separate "run as root" deployment mode PR. The former can land quickly; the latter deserves a deliberate maintainer call and tree documentation.
- If the maintainer call is that "run as root" is supported, update infrastructure/deployment/NODE.md to describe both modes and their trade-offs.
- Confirm the secrets path for the UI gateway token field.
- Add a startup warning when running as root with the broad default allowlist, so operators are explicitly aware of what they're getting.

The claude-local rate-limit reclassification is a clean improvement and would land fine on its own. The OpenClaw schema fix is also a clean adapter-level bugfix. Everything else needs a bit more deliberation.

PR #3293 Html preview
NEEDS_REVIEW high open PENDING by @KhabarovaNina · 2026-04-10T11:45:55Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: high · commit: 0aba8bc7

> [!WARNING]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review. However, this review raises a security boundary concern that should be addressed before merge.

### Summary

The product direction is good — inline HTML report preview fits the "tasks are the communication channel" and "progressive disclosure" principles, and this builds naturally on the html-report skill in #3292. But the current implementation crosses a trust boundary without enough care: agent-generated HTML is rendered in the Paperclip UI origin with a CSP that allows inline scripts and no iframe sandboxing. That's a cross-site scripting vector.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Inline report preview in issue chat | Rich artifact rendering in the task UI | "Tasks are the communication channel" + progressive disclosure | ✅ Aligned |
| Company-scoped route auth | assertCompanyAccess on the new endpoint | Multi-company isolation | ✅ Aligned |
| CSP on served HTML | default-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline' data: blob: | "Governance-first" — agent output is untrusted input | ⚠️ Conflict |
| Iframe sandboxing | No sandbox attribute on the preview iframe | Trust boundary between agent output and the Paperclip UI origin | ⚠️ Conflict |
| File-level authorization | Any board user in a company can fetch any .html in any workspace | "Every mutation is auditable" and least-privilege implied | ❓ Partial |
| Filesystem path disclosure | debug: { checkedPaths } in 404 response | Information disclosure — minor but not needed | ❓ Partial |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — communication via tasks
- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — governance enforced at server layer, agent output is untrusted
- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — service/route split and authz patterns

</details>

### Security concerns (must address before merge)

1. CSP allows inline scripts. The response sets:


    Content-Security-Policy: default-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline' data: blob:; img-src 'self' data: blob:; style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline';

'unsafe-inline' in default-src covers script-src by inheritance, which means inline <script> tags execute. The html-report skill from #3292 explicitly forbids JavaScript in its validator, but the validator runs at skill time — the CSP here has to be the enforcement layer if anything else ever drops HTML into reports/. Fix: add an explicit script-src 'none', and tighten default-src to 'self' without 'unsafe-inline'.

2. No iframe sandboxing. The HtmlReportPreview component needs <iframe sandbox="allow-same-origin" ...> (or drop allow-same-origin entirely if the report is served with CSP blocking scripts). Without sandbox, a malicious report runs in the Paperclip UI origin with access to cookies, local storage, and any in-page state.

3. Same-origin deployment. Reports are served from /api/companies/:companyId/issues/:issueId/reports/:filename — same origin as the app. Combined with (1) and (2), this is the full XSS path. Even if the html-report skill validator is correct, defense-in-depth requires the browser-level protections.

### Other concerns

4. File-level authorization. assertCompanyAccess grants any board user access to any report in any issue workspace in the company. That may be the intended model, but it's worth confirming — an ops user who can see one issue's chat also gets enumeration over every other issue's workspace files, just by guessing filenames. The filename pattern YYYY-MM-DD-slug.html is guessable.

5. Information disclosure in 404. The debug: { checkedPaths } field leaks server filesystem layout to any client that hits a 404. Remove for production builds or gate behind a debug flag.

6. "First match wins" across candidate dirs. The endpoint checks up to ~20 candidate directories and returns the first file that exists. This is correct for a single issue but has a subtle consistency bug: if the workspace lookup returns a stale or wrong workspace (e.g., a detached project workspace with an unrelated file of the same name), the wrong report is served. Low probability, but worth a guard — e.g., require the workspace row's issueId/sourceIssueId to match.

### Recommendation

Don't block on the product direction — inline preview is the right call. But before merge:

1. Tighten CSP: default-src 'none'; img-src 'self' data:; style-src 'unsafe-inline'; base-uri 'none'; form-action 'none';
2. Add iframe sandbox: <iframe sandbox="" srcdoc={...}> or <iframe sandbox="" src={url}> — no allow-same-origin, no allow-scripts.
3. Remove the debug.checkedPaths field from the 404 response body.
4. Tighten the workspace match so the served file always corresponds to a row whose issueId/sourceIssueId matches the URL.
5. Confirm the file-level auth model with maintainers — board users should probably only see reports for issues they're already permitted to view, not every workspace file in the company.

Given the html-report skill ships inline CSS and no JS, the restricted CSP above will render the expected reports correctly while making it safe to extend the system later. Worth the extra pass before landing.

### Questions for maintainers

1. Is this a "default" skill or an optional one? The PR title says "as default skill" but the diff only adds files under skills/html-report/ — no changes to server/src/services/company-skills.ts, packages/shared/src/validators/company-skill.ts, or any auto-install/bundled-skills wiring. Either:
- "Default" is aspirational and will be wired in a follow-up — in which case consider retitling to something like "Add html-report skill" to avoid confusion.
- There's a convention-based auto-discovery from skills/ that makes this "default" by virtue of living there — if so, that's worth documenting in the tree so future skill authors know the rule.

2. Is skills/ Paperclip-core or general-purpose? The existing directory holds four Paperclip control-plane skills (paperclip, paperclip-create-agent, paperclip-create-plugin, para-memory-files). html-report is a generic agent-productivity skill that would work fine outside Paperclip. That's a boundary question: should skills/ be strictly for Paperclip-meta skills (things that teach agents how to operate inside Paperclip) and general productivity skills should live elsewhere (separate repo, community skills marketplace, plugin)? Or is skills/ becoming a general first-party skill library? Whichever answer, it's worth recording in the tree so the next PR doesn't have to re-litigate.

3. Python test coverage. The PR ships 615 + 411 lines of Python (build_report.py, validate_html.py) with no visible test files. The validator is a security boundary — worth adding tests that exercise the negative examples in examples/bad-*.json to prove the validator rejects them.

### Recommendation

Don't block on the design — the skill is well-scoped and the security posture (inline CSS only, no JS, content whitelist, separate validator script) is the right shape. But before landing:

- Clarify the "default" claim in the PR title/description and the maintenance plan for skill registration.
- Get a maintainer call on whether skills/ is a control-plane-only directory or a general first-party library, and document that decision in the tree.
- Add Python tests for the validator that cover the bad-external-css.json and bad-script.json negative examples.

Path: skills/html-report/scripts/build_report.py

Comment:
_HREF_SAFE_RE accepts malformed https: URLs

The regex ^(https:|mailto:|#|/) requires only the https: prefix, so a URL like https:evil.com/path (no //) passes validation and ends up in the rendered HTML. Browsers typically treat https:path as a path-relative URL, producing a broken link rather than an XSS vector, but it silently violates the stated policy of "Only https:// URLs." The same gap exists in validate_html.py's scheme check (line 152–158 there), so malformed URLs can survive the post-render validation pass too.

suggestion
_HREF_SAFE_RE = re.compile(r"^(https://|mailto:|#|/)")

How can I resolve this? If you propose a fix, please make it concise.

Comment:
E200 check has an undocumented data: URI exemption for <link>

The guard if v.startswith("data:"): continue silently allows <link rel="stylesheet" href="data:text/css,...">, which could inject arbitrary CSS into the document. The policy (SKILL.md rule 4) forbids all external resources and doesn't carve out a data: exception for <link>. The ALLOWED_TAGS list provides a second line of defence (since link is absent, it triggers E400), but the E200 logic itself is inconsistent with the stated policy and could become a real gap if link were ever added to ALLOWED_TAGS.

PR #3291 fix(agents): make opencode_local model probe non-blocking on agent create
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open PENDING by @Peacetongue · 2026-04-10T10:45:29Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · commit: 663720c0

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

The fix unblocks a real and painful onboarding failure (opencode binary segfaults under Rosetta). But softening a validation error into a warning log sits in direct tension with two load-bearing tree decisions: "surface problems, don't hide them" and "no silent auto-recovery". The trade-off deserves an explicit maintainer call before landing.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Unblock flaky probe | Let agent creation succeed when probe throws | "Surface problems, don't hide them" (product/NODE.md) | ❓ Partial |
| Demote error to warn | throw unprocessable(...) → logger.warn(...) | "No silent auto-recovery" — the tree explicitly favors bubbling failures to the actor | ❓ Partial |
| Lazy re-validation path | /adapters/opencode_local/models catches the same config at first run | Task-system assumes issues surface where the work happens — acceptable fallback | ✅ Aligned |
| Keep instrumentation | logger.warn still logs stack + adapterType + companyId | Auditability — operators can still trace | ✅ Aligned |
| Probe can't distinguish flaky vs. real misconfig | Both paths get demoted | The server can't tell them apart — this means real misconfigs also get deferred | ⚠️ Conflict |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — "Surface problems, don't hide them" (decision #6)
- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — "No automatic recovery, no automatic reassignment"
- [adapters/opencode-local/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/opencode-local/NODE.md) — adapter lifecycle and validation contract

</details>

### Questions for maintainers

1. Can the user see the warning? A logger.warn lives in server logs that most end users never look at. If an agent is created with a genuinely broken opencode config, the user sees "success" at create-time and then a failure at first run. That's the scenario the tree explicitly calls out as the anti-pattern. Consider: return 200 with a structured warnings: [{code, message}] field in the response body so the UI can show an inline "probe failed, here's why" banner — keeps onboarding unblocked AND surfaces the problem.

2. Is there a narrower fix? Two alternatives that address the root cause instead of the symptom:
- Detect Rosetta and skip the probe: check for the x86_64 arch running under arm64e kernel (macOS) and short-circuit the probe with a specific "probe skipped on Rosetta" log line. Users on normal arm64 or amd64 still get the pre-flight validation.
- Retry the probe: if the flakiness is intermittent (the PR says "intermittently"), 2-3 retries with small backoff would fix flakiness without demoting real failures.

3. Does the UI show the warning? Worth confirming the onboarding flow can render a structured warning alongside "agent created". If not, this fix makes the bug invisible to end users even when the probe surfaces a genuine misconfig.

### Recommendation

Don't block on unblocking the Rosetta use case — it's a real pain. But before landing this exact fix, consider:

1. Picking a root-cause path (Rosetta detection, retry, or opt-in probe) that preserves create-time validation for honest failures.
2. If that's not feasible in this PR's scope, then at least return the warning in the API response body so the UI can surface it — demoting to server logs alone violates the "surface problems" principle in practice, even if the error is technically still observable.
3. Either way, add a test case for a genuinely invalid opencode config (not just a flaky probe) to prove the lazy-validation path catches it at first run.

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: b853ad7a

Aligned with context tree. No concerns.

Excellent fix. The author correctly identified that listAdapterModels(type) and detectAdapterModel(type) ignore companyId entirely — the assertCompanyAccess gate was guarding nothing and silently breaking the onboarding dropdown. Replacing it with assertBoard matches the tree's "Unified API, Different Authorization" pattern: the auth check reflects what data is actually exposed, not what the URL looks like.

What makes this PR stand out is the careful scoping discipline: POST /test-environment is explicitly left strict because it resolves per-company secrets via secretService.normalizeAdapterConfigForPersistence / resolveAdapterConfigForRuntime — loosening that one would be a real cross-company leak. Drawing that exact line, and explaining it in both the PR description and an inline test comment, is the right level of care for an auth change.

Test coverage is thoughtful too — the 95-line test file explicitly notes the local_implicit god-mode bypass and constructs realistic remote session-board actors to exercise the cross-company path. This closes a subtle test gap where default createApp() would have hidden the fix.

Also worth noting: this is yet another instance of the "silent failure" pattern I've been flagging in recent items (#3282, #3215, #3207, #3284). The 403 → empty dropdown with no clear error is the exact anti-pattern the tree's "surface problems, don't hide them" principle calls out. Worth a general audit: any endpoint gated by assertCompanyAccess that doesn't actually read companyId in its handler is likely misscoped for the same reason.

googlarz · 2026-04-10T11:21:16Z mentions-gardener references-verdict addresses-review

Thanks @serenakeyitan — I went through each of the 3 concerns. TL;DR: the PR template is now filled (it was updated right after your bot's review snapshot at 3893420c), and the coordination/placement concerns aren't actually what they look like.

### 1. PR template

Updated to the full CONTRIBUTING.md template (Thinking Path + What Changed + Why + Verification + Risks + Model Used + Checklist + Greptile follow-up) via browser edit at ~11:10Z — your bot's review was at ~10:30Z so that section is stale. Should be clean on @gardener re-review.

### 2. Core vs plugin placement

I looked at what actually lives in each layer before answering:

- Existing agent-scoped state tables in core: agent_task_sessions, agent_runtime_state, agent_api_keys, agent_config_revisions, agent_instructions. All small fixed-schema agent-lifecycle state, all in packages/db/src/schema/ + server/src/services/. Not plugins.
- What plugins actually do: see packages/plugins/examples/* — external integrations (file storage, notifications, etc.), each with its own manifest, no ability to declare new core DB tables or mount routes under /agents/:id/….
- What this PR creates: a small fixed-schema agent-scoped primitive with pg_trgm indexes, assertAgentIdentity gating, and a 500 rows × 4 KB/agent hard cap. No retrieval augmentation, no embeddings, no external services.

Putting this in plugins would require the plugin SDK to own schemas + indexes + route-layer auth guards + FK cascades to agents and companies. That's a much bigger change than what plugins currently do.

If you see this as "a knowledge base", I'd push back on that framing — it's literally a per-agent sticky-notes table with keyword search, no smarter than issue_comments (which is also in core).

### 3. Coordination with #3250

I diffed the file lists and there's zero overlap at the schema/route/service layer:

| | #3289 (this PR) | #3250 (mempalace) |
|---|---|---|
| Tables | agent_memories | memory_bindings, memory_binding_targets, memory_operations |
| Routes | /agents/:id/memories | /memory-bindings, /memory-operations |
| Service dir | server/src/services/agent-memories.ts | server/src/services/memory-adapters/{mempalace,para}.ts + memory-hooks.ts |
| Plugin SDK | no touch | adds MemoryAdapter, MemoryScope, hydration/capture types |
| Search | pg_trgm keyword | semantic via ChromaDB / file |
| Driver | agent (explicit save/search calls) | framework (pre-run hydration, post-run capture, prompt injection) |
| LLM calls | none | embeddings for vector search |
| Size | +1,183 lines | +7,361 lines, 43 files |

These are different primitives at different layers, not two implementations of the same thing. #3289 is "agent-controlled explicit notes"; #3250 is "framework-controlled retrieval-augmented context". A well-designed system likely wants both — an agent that wants to explicitly remember "user prefers French" should not need to wait for a semantic-search adapter pipeline.

Per your own table, this PR is ✅ aligned on 4 of 6 axes (auth, isolation, audit, resource bounding) — the only ❓ is the core/plugin call and the only ⚠️ is the "two memory subsystems" framing which I think is a misread of #3250's scope. Happy to coordinate with @davison if the maintainers want a formal decision recorded in the tree, but I don't think either PR should be blocked on the other.

cc @davison — do you see any actual overlap I'm missing?

davison · 2026-04-10T13:27:57Z mentions-gardener

hey 👋🏻

Not sure about the overlap, haven't looked in great detail at what this is providing but there seems to be some slight similarity of intent. I think the obvious point that the gardner plugin just missed completely is that the one I created is more about token cost than fact retrieval. The injection from a mempalace store is an attempt to add better context to the current run, it's not targeted fact retrieval. Feels more complementary than competitive.

With mempalace and my PR (which is still evolving), the interaction is transparent and injects relevant compressed content into the agent's heartbeat or run, and then transparently saves the entire transcript back at the end. The next part of it, which I think will be the more valuable part, is that this gets extended to agent instructions, paperclip API documents and other resources that the agent is presented with at the start of a run and which costs so many tokens to process every time.

But mine comes with a cost (the bit of gardeners analysis that I agree with) in having to setup and manage a sidecar to get this benefit. Their should be choices about what paperclip users want to adopt for their particular case. This plugin and PR looks good.

Are you on the paperclip discord? I'm going to post to the #dev channel there shortly about it. I'll cc you on it (let me have your username if not the same as your github. On discord I'm autistic shark.

googlarz · 2026-04-10T14:26:39Z mentions-gardener

Thanks @davison — and yes, that framing is exactly right. Your read is the one I'd hoped a human would land on: token-cost-driven automatic context injection (mempalace) and agent-driven explicit fact recall (this PR) are two halves of the same problem, not competitors. Gardener saw "memory" twice and pattern-matched to overlap without reading what each primitive actually does.

If anything they compose cleanly. An agent that learns "user prefers French" today has no way to pin it durably — mempalace's compressed context injection is optimizing for recency and relevance across a big corpus, so that single short fact can easily get summarized away or fall off the window. paperclipMemorySave gives the agent an explicit "don't forget this" primitive it can call when it KNOWS something matters. The two don't need to know about each other — mempalace can read from agent_memories as just another content source if it wants to, or not, and it still works.

The direction you mentioned (extending context injection to agent instructions + Paperclip API docs + other run-start resources) is the genuinely high-value next step — those are the biggest per-run fixed costs and the ones that hurt most at scale. Looking forward to seeing where mempalace goes there.

I'm not on the Paperclip Discord yet, so feel free to just @ me on GitHub (or reply here) if you want me in on any follow-up discussion — happy to coordinate on whether it makes sense for agent_memories to eventually implement a MemoryAdapter interface from your plugin SDK work, so the explicit-save primitive can plug into the same composition surface the sidecar adapters use.

PR #3284 fix(issues): use resolved UUID instead of identifier in wakeup payloads
ALIGNED low open PENDING by @kbecking · 2026-04-10T09:35:25Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: 7f7157a3

Aligned with context tree. No concerns.

Clean 9-line bug fix. Three wakeup payloads in routes/issues.ts were passing req.params.id (the human-readable identifier like AIU-67) instead of the already-resolved issue.id UUID, silently breaking @-mention wakeups and comment-triggered wakeups — agents never woke up for mentions. Adjacent code for assignment-wake already used the correct pattern, so this fix brings all wakeup sites into consistency.

This bug is the 4th instance of the same root pattern I've flagged in recent items (#3282 silent filter, #3215 orphaned processes, #3207 silent cleanup): the control plane fails silently rather than surfacing the problem, which the tree explicitly calls out as an anti-pattern. The fix is correct in its current scope, but consider two follow-ups as separate tasks:

1. Add a loud error log or activity event when the heartbeat service fails to resolve an issueId — a silent miss should be observable.
2. A route-level integration test for @-mention wakeups would prevent regression. The PR author notes this would require a full HTTP test harness; worth the investment given how load-bearing inter-agent communication is.

DeadlySilent · 2026-04-12T04:11:59Z references-verdict

Confirmed this is still reproducible on our side, and it appears to have been masked by #3407 until we patched around the routine lock conflict.

After stabilizing routine dispatch behavior (the #3407 class of failure), this inbox visibility problem became clearly observable again.

## Fresh verification (2026-04-12)
For the same assignee + status filter:

- GET /api/companies/{companyId}/issues?assigneeAgentId={agentId}&status=todo,in_progress,blocked → 1
- GET /api/companies/{companyId}/issues?assigneeAgentId={agentId}&status=todo,in_progress,blocked&includeRoutineExecutions=true → 16
- GET /api/companies/{companyId}/issues?assigneeAgentId={agentId}&status=todo,in_progress,blocked&originKind=routine_execution → 15

So routine execution issues are present and queryable, but hidden by default list behavior unless explicitly included.

## Why this still blocks production routine flows
Agents relying on /api/agents/me/inbox-lite miss routine-origin work after the initial wake context is gone, so recurring pipelines can stall despite in-progress assignments existing.

If maintainers agree, we can open a tiny PR that updates /agents/me/inbox-lite to pass includeRoutineExecutions: true while leaving board/default issue lists unchanged.

PR #3280 feat(goals): automatic verification loop for acceptance criteria
ALIGNED low closed AUTHOR WITHDRAWN by @googlarz · 2026-04-10T08:38:28Z → gardener comment 1 engaging 1 other

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: 6a3ca993

Upgraded from NEEDS_REVIEW · medium. Aligned with context tree. No blocking concerns.

The new commit (6a3ca993 — "fix(goals): audit every verification state transition") is a thorough and well-crafted response to the primary blocker from the prior review. Every verification state transition now writes an activity_log entry:

- goal.verification_requested — when a new cycle starts; captures attempt number, manual vs auto, criteria count
- goal.achieved — the critical governance-level transition, explicitly tagged via: "verification_outcome" so it's distinguishable from other achievement paths
- goal.verification_incomplete — missing criteria with their IDs
- goal.verification_unclear — audit even for "don't count as failure" cases, which is exactly right (the tree's "surface problems" principle covers ambiguous outcomes, not just failures)
- goal.verification_failed — failing criterion IDs and the follow-up issue ID

The VerificationActor type is well-designed. System stand-in for the auto-fire hook path, real actor threaded through for manual/issue-completion paths, with a clear comment explaining the semantics: "the audit actor for verification-driven goal transitions is the agent (or user) who PATCHed the triggering issue to done... semantically right for both branches." That's exactly the tree's "every mutation is logged with actor, action, and outcome" principle applied cleanly.

The inline comment on the goal.achieved entry deserves a specific callout: "The ACHIEVED transition is the critical auditable event here. It moves a goal from pending/active to achieved without direct human approval (per the tree's governance semantics) — the audit row captures which verification issue drove it and who was acting." That's the right framing — the PR author is treating auto-achievement as something the Board can retroactively review rather than pre-approve, and making sure the audit trail supports that.

### Residual notes (not blocking)

Two of the three questions from the prior review are still open, but neither blocks merge:

1. Is auto goal achieved a V1 governance gate? — This is a tree-docs question, not a code question. The PR now makes the transition auditable, so if the Board decides later that auto-achievement should require approval, that's a straightforward follow-up. Worth recording the decision in product/governance/NODE.md as either "auto-achievement is in-scope for V1, audit covers it" or "auto-achievement requires a new approval gate" — either answer is fine.

2. Document the verification_outcome fenced infostring in the tree. The custom json verification_outcome fence is a load-bearing agent contract that future adapters and prompt authors need to know about. Worth a short note under product/task-system/ or adapters/ describing the format so it's discoverable without reading the goal-verification source.

Neither should block this PR.

googlarz · 2026-04-10T12:49:07Z mentions-gardener references-verdict addresses-review

Thanks @serenakeyitan — good catch on the activity-log gap. One real code fix + two maintainer-call items:

### 1. Activity-log coverage → fixed in 6a3ca993

You were right: applyVerificationOutcome was flipping goal.status = achieved + stamping verifiedAt with zero audit trail, and maybeCreateVerificationIssue's goal-side update (attempts++, verificationIssueId, status=pending) was also unlogged. The only existing log was a broken goal.verification_requested call in the manual-retrigger route that fired unconditionally — even on skipped results.

Centralized all verification auditing inside the service. Now writes one audit row per terminal state transition:

| Action | When | Details captured |
|---|---|---|
| goal.verification_requested | maybeCreateVerificationIssue successfully creates the verification issue | verificationIssueId, attemptNumber, manualTrigger, criteriaCount, ownerAgentId |
| goal.achieved | applyVerificationOutcome passed verdict flips status | verificationIssueId, criteriaCount, previousStatus, via="verification_outcome" |
| goal.verification_failed | failed verdict creates follow-up issue | verificationIssueId, attemptNumber, failingCriterionIds[], followUpIssueId |
| goal.verification_incomplete | incomplete verdict sets verificationStatus=failed | verificationIssueId, missingCriterionIds[], attemptNumber |
| goal.verification_unclear | unclear verdict (status stays pending) | verificationIssueId, attemptNumber |

New VerificationActor type lets the two callers thread actor context through the service. routes/goals.ts (manual retrigger) passes the resolved board/agent actor so the audit row is attributed correctly. routes/issues.ts (auto fire-and-forget hook) passes the actor from the triggering PATCH — semantically correct for both branches: the verification agent who posted the outcome in Branch A, and the issue-completing agent whose done-transition started the new cycle in Branch B.

Typecheck clean, 19 existing verification tests still pass.

### 2. Auto-achieved as a governance gate → punting to maintainers

You're right that this is a real architectural question. Right now the tree gates Hiring and CEO Strategy Approval but not goal achievement, and an agent-driven transition to achieved IS a material decision. Two reasonable postures:

- Current PR: treat agent-verified achieved as a normal audited transition, rely on the Board's "override any Agent decision" power for correction after the fact. This is what the PR ships.
- Alternative: add a new "Goal Achievement" approval gate, require Board sign-off before the status flip. Verification outcome becomes an approval payload instead of a direct mutation.

Both are defensible. I don't want to quietly broaden the scope of this PR to add a new approval kind without an explicit call from maintainers — if @paperclipai maintainers decide they want a gate, I'm happy to ship it as a stacked PR on top of this one. Leaving this as a discussion point rather than a blocker.

### 3. Document the 

json verification_outcome
fence format → minor, separate PR

Agreed the custom infostring is load-bearing and should be discoverable. Not going to sneak it into this PR's scope — will ship a small follow-up that adds a "Goal Verification Contract" section to skills/paperclip/SKILL.md (where agents actually read it) and optionally a mirror in the context tree.

---

Per your alignment table, the two ❓ partial fits (bounded auto-retry + auto goal→achieved) are now ❓/⚠️ only on the governance-gate question from #2, not on audit coverage. Happy to @gardener re-review once you're ready.

cc @paperclipai/maintainers for the #2 decision.

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: medium

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Confirmed bug that aligns with two load-bearing tree decisions. The fix as proposed is correct: the wakeup is currently misplaced in the HTTP route handler instead of the service layer, which breaks every non-HTTP caller.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Service-level wakeup | Move queueIssueAssignmentWakeup() into the service so all callers (HTTP + plugin host + CLI) trigger it | "Routes are thin HTTP handlers — parse request, call service, return response. Services contain all business logic." | ✅ Aligned |
| Plugin parity with HTTP | Plugin ctx.issues.create() must have the same side effects as the REST API | "Plugin system is first-class" — plugins extend Paperclip without forking | ✅ Aligned |
| Silent failure | Agent stays idle after assignment, no error surfaced | "Surface problems, don't hide them" — silent idle is the anti-pattern | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — Route/Service split: "thin HTTP handlers... Services contain all business logic"
- [plugins/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/plugins/NODE.md) — Capability-gated plugin access; plugin host services must honor the same invariants as core API callers
- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — Task assignment is the primary agent signaling mechanism

</details>

### Recommendation

Rather than duplicating the wakeup call in plugin-host-services.ts (the proposed fix), consider moving queueIssueAssignmentWakeup() into issueService.create() and issueService.update() themselves. This matches the tree's explicit guidance that "services are reusable (e.g., the CLI can call service logic directly for heartbeat runs)" — any future caller (CLI, cron jobs, internal scripts) will automatically get correct behavior instead of needing to remember to call the wakeup. If there is a reason the wakeup should NOT fire for certain callers, a { skipWakeup: true } option on the service is cleaner than duplicating the call everywhere it's needed.

Related items #1280 and #1063 suggest a broader pattern: several heartbeat/wakeup signals live outside the services that mutate the state they respond to. Worth considering whether the whole class of "mutation → wakeup" couplings should move into the service layer as part of this fix.

Issue #3271 Agent JWTs cannot access plugin tool endpoints (assertBoard blocks agents)
ALIGNED high open by @nullEFFORT · 2026-04-10T07:44:15Z → gardener comment

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: high · issue: #3271

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Agent JWTs being blocked from plugin tool endpoints by assertBoard directly contradicts the tree's governance decision that "the same REST API serves both the Board UI and agents — authentication determines permissions." The proposed assertBoardOrAgent fix for the two tool endpoints is the correct and architecturally expected solution.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Unified API + auth-based scoping | Replace assertBoard with assertBoardOrAgent on tool list/execute endpoints only | Governance: "Unified API, Different Authorization — same REST API serves both Board UI and agents. Authentication determines permissions: board auth has full access, agent API keys have scoped access." | ✅ Aligned |
| Agent access scope | Agents scoped to their own company via assertCompanyAccess(req, runContext.companyId) | Governance: "agent API keys have scoped access (own tasks, cost reporting, company context)"; plugin tools are execution-side tools an agent legitimately needs | ✅ Aligned |
| Plugin extensibility | Plugin tools (e.g., escalate_to_human) contributed to the runtime are inaccessible to agents | Plugin SDK: tools is a first-class client on PluginContext; PluginToolDispatcher is designed to serve agent executeTool calls. Blocking agents defeats the purpose. | ✅ Aligned |
| Board-only management routes | Install, enable, disable, and other management routes stay board-only | Governance: board has unrestricted access; only tool list/execute endpoints need loosening for agents. This is correctly scoped in the proposal. | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — "Unified API, Different Authorization" decision; board vs agent auth scoping; governance enforced at server layer
- [plugins/runtime/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/plugins/runtime/NODE.md) — PluginToolRegistry / PluginToolDispatcher: registers tools and dispatches executeTool calls from agents to plugin workers
- [plugins/sdk/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/plugins/sdk/NODE.md) — tools is a first-class PluginContext client; plugin tool contribution is an SDK-level contract with agents as the consumers

</details>

### Recommendation

This is a high-severity bug because it breaks a core tree invariant: agents are supposed to have scoped-but-real API access, and plugin tools are the primary extensibility surface. The fix is well-scoped — introducing assertBoardOrAgent on the two affected endpoints while leaving all plugin management routes board-only is exactly right. Recommend prioritizing this fix. The existing assertCompanyAccess call provides the correct isolation boundary for agent access.

Issue #3273 Plugin tool execute requires projectId but agent runs often have none
ALIGNED medium open by @nullEFFORT · 2026-04-10T07:43:48Z → gardener comment

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: medium · issue: #3273

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Requiring projectId in the plugin tool execute endpoint contradicts the tree's company-scoped isolation model, where companyId is the authoritative scope boundary and projectId is an optional context field. Removing projectId from the required validation check is the correct fix.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Scoping model | projectId should be optional in runContext; companyId is the required scope boundary | Tree: "Company-scoped isolation — all entities scoped to company_id. Never leak data across companies." projectId is not the isolation unit. | ✅ Aligned |
| Plugin tool dispatch | Plugin tool execution routes to PluginToolDispatcher which dispatches to plugin workers | PluginToolDispatcher dispatches executeTool calls to the appropriate plugin worker; projectId is passed through as context, not used for routing | ✅ Aligned |
| Agent wake-on-demand | Many agent runs have no project association (wake-on-demand) | Agent model supports "callable" as the minimum contract; no requirement for project context to trigger or run an agent | ✅ Aligned |
| Governance | Auth/access enforced at server layer | Governance: "Governance rules are control-plane invariants enforced at the server" — the fix keeps companyId required (the actual isolation boundary) while removing the spurious projectId check | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [plugins/runtime/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/plugins/runtime/NODE.md) — PluginToolDispatcher dispatches executeTool calls; PluginRegistry has pluginId scoping; no mention of projectId as a routing requirement
- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — Company-scoped isolation, governance enforced at server layer
- [product/agent-model/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/agent-model/NODE.md) — Minimum contract: "callable" — no project context required

</details>

### Recommendation

The proposed fix is correct and consistent with the architecture. Accept the change: remove !runContext.projectId from the validation guard, keep agentId, runId, and companyId required. Consider also verifying that projectId is propagated to plugin workers as optional context (not silently dropped) so plugins that care about project context still receive it when it exists.

PR #3277 feat(issues): auto-reassign issue to creator on in_review status transition
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open PENDING by @kbecking · 2026-04-10T07:43:34Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · commit: 228d1c6

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

The auto-reassign behaviour sits in tension with two load-bearing product principles: "Surface problems, don't hide them" and the explicit decision that automatic recovery is not a Paperclip responsibility. Whether the delegation handoff pattern is a special case worth carving out, or a slippery slope toward hidden orchestration logic, needs a deliberate call from the maintainers.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| No automatic recovery | Auto-reassign to creator when in_review is set — implicit side effect on a status transition | Task system: "When an agent crashes mid-task, Paperclip does not auto-reassign or auto-release the task… Recovery is manual/explicit." | ❓ Partial |
| Surface problems, don't hide them | A status change silently mutates the assignee field without any actor explicitly requesting it | Product decision 6: "No silent auto-recovery, no automatic reassignment. Good auditing and visibility let the right entity decide what to do." | ⚠️ Conflict |
| Tasks are the communication channel | Delegation handoff via in_review is a real, common pattern agents rely on | Task system: all agent communication flows through tasks; completing a sub-task and handing back is expected workflow | ✅ Aligned |
| Auditable everything | No audit-log entry for the auto-reassignment is visible in the diff | Governance: every mutation writes to activity_log; nothing should happen silently | ❓ Partial |
| Single-assignee model | Reassign to creator clears the previous assignee — no multi-assignee conflict | Task system: single-assignee is deliberate | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — "No Automatic Recovery"; all work must be explicit
- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — Product decision 6: surface problems, don't hide them
- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — "Auditable everything"; every mutation writes to activity_log
- [product/agent-model/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/agent-model/NODE.md) — Cross-team coordination via tasks; delegation pattern context

</details>

### Recommendation

Two questions for the maintainers before merging:

1. Is the in_review handoff exempt from the "no automatic reassignment" principle? The tree's rationale for that principle is about crash recovery hiding failures. A deliberate in_review transition is different in intent — but the implementation is still invisible to the task's audit trail. If this is a carve-out, document the distinction in the tree (task-system node) so future contributors don't erode it further.

2. Is the auto-reassignment logged in the activity_log? The diff shows the side-effect fires inside applyStatusSideEffects before the DB write, but it's not clear whether the resulting assignee change generates an activity_log entry. The governance principle is that every mutation is auditable. A silent assignee change — even a useful one — is a gap.

If both questions are answered yes, the verdict would flip to ALIGNED. Consider updating the task-system tree node to explicitly acknowledge the in_review handoff pattern as a sanctioned workflow shortcut.

### Summary

But the discovery route (GET /plugins/tools) has no company filtering, and opening it to agent JWTs creates a cross-company data leak that violates Paperclip's core isolation principle.

What the tree says about Claude auth:
The claude-local adapter does not manage API keys or subscription state directly. Auth is fully delegated to the Claude CLI's own credential store (see adapters/claude-local). Whether a given Claude credential is subscription-based or API-credit-based is determined by the CLI — Paperclip passes through whatever auth the CLI holds.

Context match:

| Topic | Tree node | Status |
|---|---|---|
| Claude adapter auth model | adapters/claude-local | Delegation to CLI — no Paperclip-level opinion |
| Billing/quota reporting | adapters/claude-local | Adapter reports usage from Claude stream-json output |
| API key ownership | adapters/claude-local | Out of scope for Paperclip |

Recommendation: This is a support question best answered by a maintainer or in the project's documentation/FAQ. If the answer reveals a documentation gap (e.g., subscription vs. API-credit auth modes are undocumented), consider opening a docs issue.

No tree update needed — auth delegation to the Claude CLI is already captured in adapters/claude-local.

Issue #3224 [Feature Request] Support for Gemini 3.5 and Enhanced 'Auto' Model Fallback Logic**
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open by @woohopark · 2026-04-10T04:56:35Z → gardener comment

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · issue: #3224

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

This request has two parts with different alignment profiles. Adding Gemini 3.5 to the model list is a straightforward adapter maintenance task. The "Auto" model fallback — automatically switching models when one hits a rate limit — touches the adapter boundary design and the "surface problems, don't hide them" principle, and warrants more discussion.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Gemini 3.5 model support | Add Gemini 3.5 to the model selection dropdown | Adapters expose detectModel and model listing; updating the Gemini model list when new versions ship is routine adapter maintenance | ✅ Aligned |
| Auto model fallback on rate limit | When "Auto" is selected and the current model hits quota, silently switch to another model | Tree says no quota reporting exists for the Gemini adapter ("Google's Gemini API does not expose rate-limit windows in the same way"). Also, "Surface problems, don't hide them" — silent model switching without user awareness conflicts with the visibility principle | ❓ Partial |
| Adapter boundary | Rate-limit detection and fallback logic within the Gemini adapter | Adapters own execution behavior; adding quota detection is in scope. However, automatic fallback without board visibility is a governance concern | ❓ Partial |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [adapters/gemini-local/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/gemini-local/NODE.md) — No quota reporting; model detection not currently supported; auth-required detection pattern
- [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md) — getQuotaWindows interface exists per adapter; adapter owns billing inference
- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — "Surface problems, don't hide them" — silent switching without audit log entry would violate this

</details>

### Recommendation

Gemini 3.5 support: Accept. It's a routine model list update with no architectural implications.

Auto fallback: Needs design discussion. The tree currently documents that Gemini has no quota reporting, so detecting rate limits is itself a new capability. If fallback is implemented, it should: (1) be logged as an activity event visible in the board's audit trail, not silent; (2) not be the default behavior unless the user explicitly opts in. Silent model switching without board awareness conflicts with the governance-first and visibility principles. Recommend tracking the fallback as a separate issue with a design proposal.
