Issue #3257 Built-in board notification system (email/webhook on issue assignment)
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open by @rudyjellis · 2026-04-10T04:56:33Z → gardener comment

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · issue updated: 2026-04-10T02:08:04Z

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

The feature request is valid and the underlying need is real — board users can't reliably receive out-of-band alerts when agents need intervention. However, there is a direct tension between two tree decisions that requires a deliberate maintainer call: the governance-first principle argues this belongs in core, while the "thin core, rich edges" principle says notification delivery (email/webhook) belongs in plugins.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Board governance reachability | Board users must receive alerts when agents need intervention, even if the UI is closed | Board has unrestricted oversight; "surface problems, don't hide them"; budget hard-stops notify the board | ❓ Partial |
| Core vs. plugin boundary | Requesting email/webhook notification as core infrastructure | "Thin core, rich edges" — knowledge bases, external integrations, and special surfaces go into plugins, not core | ⚠️ Conflict |
| Triggering events | assigneeUserId change, blocked status, approval created, budget threshold | Budget hard-stops already emit high-priority activity events; board notification on budget threshold is already in the governance model | ❓ Partial |
| Plugin as workaround | Reporter built a board-notify plugin using Resend | Plugin SDK supports ctx.events.on() subscriptions and ctx.http.fetch() for outbound calls — the plugin pattern works | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — "Thin core, rich edges": external integrations go into plugins; governance-first
- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — Board hard-stops and budget threshold events already defined; board oversight is non-negotiable
- [plugins/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/plugins/NODE.md) — Plugin event subscriptions and outbound HTTP via ctx.http.fetch; plugin extensibility is the designed escape hatch

</details>

### Recommendation

The maintainers need to decide: is notification delivery infrastructure (email/webhook routing) a governance primitive that belongs in core, or an integration concern that belongs in a first-party plugin? Both positions are defensible:

- Core argument: Board reachability is a safety property, not a feature. If agents can't reliably page the human, governance fails silently — which directly contradicts "surface problems, don't hide them."
- Plugin argument: Email providers (Resend, SES, SMTP), webhook formats, and filtering logic vary per operator. The "thin core, rich edges" principle exists precisely to avoid baking in opinionated integrations that not every operator wants.

A middle path worth considering: add a lightweight notification hook abstraction in core (event → configurable webhook POST) with no email logic, and ship first-party email plugins separately. This preserves the thin core while making the default experience work out of the box.

The reporter's board-notify plugin demonstrates the plugin path is viable today. If the plugin SDK has the right event hooks and capability grants, promoting a reference plugin to "bundled by default" may be the right answer rather than adding email logic to the server.

---

A Trae adapter is worth pursuing as a community contribution. The scope should be narrowed to: implement ServerAdapterModule for Trae, support task execution, and follow the existing skill injection contract. Knowledge base and cross-adapter skill exchange should be tracked as separate proposals. The tree does not have a Trae-specific node yet — if the adapter moves forward, adapters/trae-local/NODE.md should be created.

Issue #3236 Feature request: Board inbox filtering — hide agent run failures, show only actionable items
NEEDS_REVIEW medium open by @pfergi42 · 2026-04-10T04:55:35Z → gardener comment 1 other
(3 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · issue: #3236

> [!CAUTION]

| Governance board powers | Board retains unrestricted access to pause, terminate, and override any agent | Filtering the inbox is fine as long as the board can still discover and act on failures when needed | ❓ Partial |

<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

### Recommendation

The filtering direction is reasonable for a 40-agent org at scale. However, the design should keep failures visible somewhere (a separate "Agent Activity" tab is mentioned — that's the right approach), not suppressible entirely. The "option to disable failure notifications in board inbox entirely" is the one ask that conflicts with tree principles. Recommend accepting the filtering/tab-separation direction, and discussing the "disable entirely" ask with maintainers before implementing. ### Summary

Re-reviewed after HEAD update (7f5f43a2 → 6896dfb6). The architectural concern from the prior review is unchanged: the memory subsystem is still wired directly into server/src/services/memory-, server/src/routes/memory-, and heartbeat.ts — it has NOT been moved to the plugin system. The PR has grown and the implementation quality remains high (company-scoped, audited via memory_operations table, isolated sidecar failure modes, PARA fallback), but the core-vs-plugin question is still the blocker.

### What's new and what's unchanged

Unchanged between the two HEADs: architectural placement. server/src/services/memory-adapters/ (mempalace, PARA, sidecar), memory-hooks.ts, memory-operations.ts, memory-bindings.ts, routes/memory-bindings.ts, routes/memory-operations.ts, and heartbeat integration all still live in core.

Helpful new concrete comparison point: [PR #3285 (feat(plugins): add aws-file-store plugin with MinIO compose)](https://github.com/paperclipai/paperclip/pull/3285) just landed and demonstrates exactly the architectural pattern the tree calls for — it re-scoped a similar "storage-backed agent capability" feature from the CONFLICT version in #3230 into a proper first-party plugin at packages/plugins/examples/aws-file-store, using the standard plugin SDK (9 tools, lifecycle hooks, capability manifest, host-owned audit logging). That's the reference implementation for how this kind of subsystem is supposed to integrate.

### Recommendation

The two recommendations from the prior review still apply:

1. Keep in core with explicit rationale — document a new product/memory/ or updated product/agent-model/ tree node that says pre-run hydration and post-run capture are fundamental to the heartbeat protocol, analogous to cost tracking. This is a deliberate scope expansion and needs tree PR first.

2. Move to a first-party plugin — use PR #3285 as the template. The MemoryAdapter interface in packages/plugins/sdk/src/types.ts is already the right abstraction. The gap is that core currently calls adapters directly; instead, a @paperclipai/plugin-mempalace (or plugin-memory-core) would register the adapter and hook into heartbeat via the plugin event/tool system. The UI pages could live in the plugin's UI slots.

The re-review is unchanged: this is a substantial feature that is technically well-built but makes an undocumented architectural decision. Either path is defensible — the decision needs to be made deliberately, not by default.

Engaging with gardener (2)

davison · 2026-04-11T05:11:07Z mentions-gardener addresses-review

## CTO Response — Memory Subsystem Architecture

Thanks for the thorough context review. I've considered both paths and am making a deliberate architectural decision:

Memory stays in core. Here's the rationale:

### Core vs. Plugin distinction

The key architectural question is whether memory lifecycle hooks (pre-run hydration, post-run capture) are orchestration concerns or agent capabilities.

They are orchestration. Specifically:

- Pre-run hydration populates agent context before the heartbeat begins — this is system-initiated, automatic, and unconditional for agents with memory bindings. The agent never "calls" it.
- Post-run capture extracts learnings after execution completes — again system-initiated, part of the run lifecycle.
- This is analogous to cost tracking and budget enforcement — also in core, also system-initiated lifecycle hooks that agents don't opt into.

### Why this differs from aws-file-store (PR #3285)

PR #3285 is the right pattern for agent-initiated tools — the agent decides when to read/write files, and the plugin registers tools the agent can call. File storage is an optional capability.

Memory hooks are the inverse: the system decides when to hydrate and capture, not the agent. Moving this to a plugin would mean the heartbeat depends on an optional plugin for a non-optional behavior — that's architecturally worse, not better.

### Where the adapter boundary lives

The MemoryAdapter interface (write, query, get, forget) IS the plugin boundary. Mempalace (ChromaDB-backed MCP) and PARA (file-based) are swappable backends registered through adapter configuration. The core owns the lifecycle; adapters own the storage.

### Documentation path

I'll document this in a docs/architecture/memory.md that captures:
- Memory as a core orchestration concern (not an agent capability)
- The adapter interface as the extensibility boundary
- Why the heartbeat lifecycle hooks are non-optional

This is a deliberate scope expansion of core, not an accidental one.

PR #3237 feat(skills): GitHub PAT support for private skill repos + delete by source
ALIGNED medium open PENDING by @cpfarhood · 2026-04-10T04:51:22Z → gardener comment 1 engaging 6 other

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: medium · commit: 1956ccd

> [!WARNING]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

This PR adds GitHub PAT support for private skill repos and a bulk delete-by-source endpoint. Both features are well-aligned with the adapter abstraction, governance-first, and company-scoped isolation principles. Severity is medium because PAT handling at the boundary between client and secrets vault is a sensitive pattern — the implementation looks correct but warrants a human eye on the credential lifecycle.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Secrets / PAT storage | PAT accepted at import time, stored as encrypted company secret via secretService, referenced by ID in skill metadata | Governance-first: audit trails on all mutations — PATCH /:skillId/auth logs skill_auth_updated/skill_auth_removed, import logs via existing activity system. Secrets vault already established. | ✅ Aligned |
| Company-scoped isolation | deleteBySource and updateSkillAuth both scope to companyId; route-level assertCanMutateCompanySkills guard present | All entities must be scoped to company_id — enforced at both route and DB query layers | ✅ Aligned |
| Adapter abstraction | Auth token threaded through ghFetch → all GitHub resolution helpers; retrieved from vault on subsequent calls | Agent runtimes connect through common adapter interface; auth wiring is internal to the adapter layer | ✅ Aligned |
| PAT not logged in audit details | logActivity for skill_auth_updated records only slug, not the token value | Governance: full audit trails required, but logging secrets would be a security anti-pattern — the current approach (log action + skill id, not credential) is correct | ✅ Aligned |
| Secret not deleted on PAT clear | updateSkillAuth(null) clears sourceAuthSecretId from metadata but leaves the underlying secret row | Minor lifecycle gap: orphaned secret rows accumulate. No tree decision violated, but worth a follow-up cleanup task | ⚠️ Minor gap |
| Bulk delete by source (UI) | Trash icon on source label triggers DELETE /by-source — removes all skills from a source without per-skill confirmation of agent usage | Pre-check atomicity is correct (service checks all skills before deleting any). Dialog warns user. No tree conflict. | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — governance-first, audit trails on every mutation, hard-stops as core (not optional)
- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — route/service split, secrets vault, authentication patterns

</details>

### Recommendation

Approve with one follow-up: the orphaned secret on PAT clear is a minor hygiene issue (not a blocker). Consider opening a follow-up issue to delete the underlying secret when updateSkillAuth(null) is called and no other skill references it.

PR #3252 feat: board escalation - boardAttentionAt field, inbox filters, and noise reduction
ALIGNED medium closed AUTHOR WITHDRAWN by @yunwei-zh · 2026-04-10T04:49:15Z → gardener comment
(2 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: medium · commit: b3f660b

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

This PR adds a boardAttentionAt escalation primitive that lets agents signal "I need a human" without side-effecting issue status or assignee, and cleans up Board inbox noise by adding focused filter categories (Escalated, In Review, Assigned to me), hiding terminal-status issues from the Board default view, and moving the "Hide agent failures" toggle into an Options popover. The changes are well-aligned with Paperclip's governance-first and surface-problems-don't-hide-them principles, and the progressive-disclosure approach (amber banner in issue detail + filter categories in inbox) fits the thin-core/rich-edges pattern.

Note on Greptile's P1/P2 findings: After reading the diff directly, the Greptile P1 ("dismiss does not clear escalation globally") and P2 ("missing filter categories / localStorage persistence") are inaccurate for this version of the PR. The archiveIssueMutation.mutationFn correctly calls issuesApi.update(id, { boardAttentionAt: null }) before archiving when the issue is escalated. The escalations, in_review_issues, and assigned_to_me filter categories exist in InboxCategoryFilter (moved to ui/src/lib/inbox.ts), and saveInboxCategoryFilter is called on every filter change. The escalation badge test is also present in inbox.test.ts. Greptile appears to have evaluated an earlier version or missed the type definition move.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Governance / Board control surface | Add a channel for agents to signal "I need a human" without side-effecting task status | Governance node: "The Board is not just an approval gate — it is a live control surface. The human can intervene at any level at any time." Board powers always available. | ✅ Aligned |
| Auditable everything | boardAttentionAt is a field on the issue, mutated via the same PATCH endpoint; clears globally when board user dismisses | Governance node: "Every mutation writes to activity_log. The system is designed so that nothing happens silently." | ✅ Aligned |
| Board-only clear guard | Non-board actors return 403 when attempting to set boardAttentionAt: null | Governance node: "Governance rules are control-plane invariants enforced at the server, not at the adapter or agent level." | ✅ Aligned |
| Tasks as communication channel | Agents escalate via boardAttentionAt on an existing issue rather than through a side-channel | Task system node: "All agent communication flows through the task system. There is no separate messaging or chat system." | ✅ Aligned |
| Surface problems, don't hide them | Amber escalation banner in issue detail, red dot badge for escalations, terminal-status Board cleanup | Tree principle: "Surface problems, don't hide them" | ✅ Aligned |
| Progressive disclosure | Escalation summary in inbox badge → filter categories → amber banner in issue detail with Clear action | Tree principle: "Progressive disclosure (summary → checklist → raw logs)" | ✅ Aligned |
| Company-scoped isolation | No cross-company data; boardQueueUserId filter is scoped via companyId from the existing route guard | Tree decision: "All entities scoped to company_id. Never leak data across companies." | ✅ Aligned |
| Dismiss side-effect risk | If issuesApi.update succeeds but archiveFromInbox fails, escalation is already cleared — intentional per PR | PR documents this as "Acceptable — the issue stays visible and the user can re-dismiss." This is a reasonable UX tradeoff; not a governance concern. | ✅ Aligned |
| Clear button visible to all actors on IssueDetail | Board-only guard is server-side; agents viewing their own issue detail could see a "Clear" button that returns 403 on click | Governance: "Unified API, Different Authorization." The server guard is correct, but the UI shows a control that silently fails for non-board users — a minor UX inconsistency worth noting. | ❓ Partial |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — Board powers, approval gates, budget controls, audit trail requirements
- [product/task-system/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/task-system/NODE.md) — Tasks as the communication channel; no side-channel messaging

</details>

### Recommendation

Ship with one minor follow-up to consider: the "Clear" button in IssueDetail.tsx is rendered for all viewers of an escalated issue, but it silently fails (403) for non-board actors. Since agents can view their own issues, they'll see a button they can't use. A lightweight client-side guard (hide the button unless the current session is a board user) would be consistent with Paperclip's "surface problems, don't hide them" principle — surface the escalation state, but don't show a control that isn't available. This is low-severity and can be done as a follow-up.

PR #3262 feat: Company Files — scoped knowledge base with UI, API, and agent integration
CONFLICT high open PENDING by @vinccirom · 2026-04-10T04:47:44Z → gardener comment 1 engaging
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: \CONFLICT\ · severity: \high\ · commit: \a4690b3\

> [!WARNING]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

This PR adds a knowledge base as a first-class core feature (DB table, 10 REST endpoints, heartbeat injection across all 6 adapters, UI page), which directly contradicts three explicit tree decisions: knowledge bases belong in plugins not the core control plane, Paperclip is explicitly "not a knowledge base", and knowledge base was deferred from V1 scope.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Knowledge base in core | Adds knowledge_entries table, service, and 10 REST routes directly into server core | "Thin core, rich edges. Knowledge bases… go into plugins — not the core control plane." (product/NODE.md) | ⚠️ Conflict |
| Paperclip identity | Positions knowledge base as a first-class Paperclip feature | "Paperclip is explicitly not: …a knowledge base…" (product/NODE.md) | ⚠️ Conflict |
| V1 scope | Ships as a new core feature | "Explicitly deferred from V1: …knowledge base…" (product/NODE.md) | ⚠️ Conflict |
| Adapter integration | Injects knowledge manifest into all 6 adapter heartbeat prompts | Adapter abstraction is aligned; the question is whether the data source should be core vs plugin | ❓ Partial |
| Company-scoped isolation | All queries are scoped to company_id; auth follows existing assertCompanyAccess pattern | Company-scoped isolation (engineering/NODE.md) | ✅ Aligned |
| Audit trail | All mutations call logActivity with before/after details | Governance-first; every mutation logged (product/NODE.md) | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — Product strategy, anti-requirements, V1 scope; explicitly lists knowledge base as out-of-scope for core and for V1
- [engineering/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/NODE.md) — Backend architecture; service-oriented pattern; company-scoped isolation

</details>

### Recommendation

This work is solid in implementation quality — the scoping, audit trail, and adapter integration are all well-executed. The conflict is with where it lives, not whether it should exist.

Two paths forward:

1. Move to a plugin (tree-aligned): Extract the knowledge base into a plugin using the Plugin SDK. The heartbeat injection via renderPaperclipKnowledgePrompt and the knowledge service logic can live in a plugin that registers routes, injects into heartbeat context, and owns the DB migration. The tree's "thin core, rich edges" decision exists precisely to protect the control plane from scope creep.

2. Update the tree first (if the team has decided knowledge base is now core): If product has deliberately changed direction on this, update product/NODE.md to remove the anti-requirement and un-defer knowledge base from V1 scope — then land this PR. That PR should be discussed and merged before this code lands.

Either way, this PR should not merge until the conflict is resolved. The tree is the decision record; the code should follow from it.

Engaging with gardener (1)

vinccirom · 2026-04-10T06:11:18Z mentions-gardener addresses-review

## Response to gardener context review

We investigated the plugin path thoroughly. After an exhaustive audit of the Plugin SDK (41 capabilities, 13 UI slot types, all data persistence APIs), the plugin architecture cannot support a company file system without significant degradation:

| Requirement | Core | Plugin SDK | Impact |
|-------------|------|-----------|--------|
| Folder hierarchy with referential integrity | ✅ Self-referencing parentId FK | ❌ Flat JSONB with parentId field | No cascade delete, no tree integrity |
| Relational data model (FKs to documents, assets, agents) | ✅ knowledge_entries table | ❌ plugin_entities JSONB blobs only | No referential integrity, no indexes |
| Document revision tracking | ✅ Reuses documents + document_revisions | ❌ Manual versioning in JSONB | No audit trail on document changes |
| File upload + storage | ✅ multer + StorageService | ❌ "Future scope" per plugin spec | No binary files at all |
| Agent context awareness | ✅ Lightweight manifest in heartbeat | ❌ Agent must explicitly call tool | Agents don't know files exist unless they search |
| Department scoping via org tree | ✅ Recursive CTE on agents.reportsTo | ❌ No SQL access | Cannot efficiently resolve subtrees |
| Custom REST API (10 endpoints) | ✅ Express routes | ❌ Only webhook + bridge proxy | No direct API |

### The case for core

The gardener classifies this as "a knowledge base." It isn't. It's a company file system — structured folders and documents scoped to company, department, and agent.

Every real organization has files. Not a knowledge base product, not a wiki, not Notion — just a structured place where persistent company files live. This is as fundamental as having an org chart or a budget. A company without a file system is incomplete infrastructure.

- Org charts are core → they define who reports to whom
- Budgets are core → they define spending limits
- Approval policies are core → they define governance gates
- Company files should be core → they define everything else the company needs to persist

The plugin system can't provide this because it was designed for external integrations (Linear sync, GitHub webhooks) — not organizational primitives. The gaps (no schema, no hierarchy, no uploads, no revision tracking) prove the point.

### Tree PR

Per the gardener's guidance, we've opened a PR to update the context tree:

[serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree#1](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/pull/1) — proposes distinguishing "general-purpose knowledge base / wiki" (still deferred) from "company file system" (foundational infrastructure).

Happy to hear the team's perspective.

PR #3265 Fix plugin page routes doubling company prefix on company switch
NEEDS_REVIEW medium closed AUTHOR WITHDRAWN by @harperaa · 2026-04-10T04:46:00Z → gardener comment 1 other
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

> [!WARNING]
> gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · commit: ccd7776

---

## Summary

This PR is titled as a bug fix for plugin page route prefix-doubling, and that fix is correct and aligned. However, the PR bundles four substantial and largely unrelated changes under a misleading title: a new BastionClaw adapter (filesystem IPC + SQLite polling), a company-level kill switch (pause/resume), a heartbeat model override feature, and the actual bug fix. The BastionClaw adapter introduces a new architectural pattern not recorded in the context tree, and there is a SQL injection risk in the adapter's polling loop.

---

## Context Match

| Area | Tree | PR | Match |
|---|---|---|---|
| Plugin page route fix (company-routes.ts) | Plugin extensibility is core; routing correctness required | Correctly strips company prefix for any non-global segment | ✅ Aligned |
| Company pause/resume (kill switch) | Governance: "Board can pause/resume any Agent immediately"; company lifecycle has paused status | Board-only POST /:companyId/pause + POST /:companyId/resume, cancels active runs | ✅ Aligned |
| Heartbeat skips paused companies | Company lifecycle: "Paused companies stop all heartbeats" | tickTimers now queries paused companies and skips their agents | ✅ Aligned |
| BastionClaw adapter pattern | Tree lists gateway adapters as WebSocket-based (openclaw-gateway); "gateway adapters connect to a remote agent over WebSocket" | BastionClaw uses filesystem IPC + SQLite polling — not WebSocket | ⚠️ New Territory |
| Heartbeat model override | No tree node records adapter-level model override at heartbeat invocation | heartbeat.model added to heartbeat policy, injected into runtimeConfig on timer runs only | ⚠️ New Territory |

---

## Issues

### 1. SQL injection risk in BastionClaw adapter (medium severity)

In packages/adapters/bastionclaw/src/server/execute.ts, the task poll query interpolates taskId directly into an SQL string with only single-quote escaping:

```ts
SELECT status, result, error, duration_ms FROM task_run_logs WHERE task_id = '${taskId.replace(/'/g, "''")}' ORDER BY run_at DESC LIMIT 1
```

taskId is constructed as paperclip-${ctx.runId} where ctx.runId comes from the server. While the server controls runId today, this pattern bypasses parameterized queries and creates a brittle trust assumption. The sqlite3 CLI used here supports parameterized queries via -cmd. This should use a parameterized form or at minimum assert that taskId contains only safe characters before interpolation.

### 2. PR bundles four unrelated changes under a misleading title (low-medium)

The title "Fix plugin page routes doubling company prefix on company switch" covers only ~10 lines of the 3,800-line diff. The rest introduces: a new adapter, a company kill switch feature, a heartbeat model override, GitHub issue templates, and a SECURITY.md. Bundling makes review harder and commit history less useful. These should be separate PRs.

### 3. BastionClaw adapter pattern is not in the tree (new territory)

The adapters tree node defines two patterns: local (spawns a child process) and gateway (WebSocket). BastionClaw uses a third pattern: filesystem IPC + SQLite polling. The adapter writes a JSON task file to a shared directory and polls a SQLite DB for completion. This is a novel integration pattern with meaningful tradeoffs (local-only, polling latency, SQLite lock sensitivity) that should be captured in the tree before the adapter ships, so future adapters don't re-litigate this design.

### 4. models: [] in BastionClaw index.ts

packages/adapters/bastionclaw/src/index.ts exports models: []. The tree notes that adapters report model info via detectModel. If BastionClaw can detect the model from the Claude instance it dispatches to, this should be wired up rather than left empty.

---

## Tree Nodes Referenced

- adapters/NODE.md — local vs gateway pattern, ServerAdapterModule interface
- adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md — gateway adapter precedent
- product/governance/NODE.md — board powers, pause/resume, budget hard-stops
- product/company-model/NODE.md — company lifecycle (active/paused/archived)
- product/NODE.md — control plane principles

---

## Recommendation

The routing fix and the governance/heartbeat changes are aligned and look correct. The BastionClaw adapter is new territory worth flagging:

1. Fix the SQL injection before merge — use parameterized queries or character-validation on taskId.
2. Confirm the IPC+SQLite pattern is intentional and draft a adapters/bastionclaw/NODE.md tree node capturing the design rationale and constraints (local-only, SQLite polling, requires BastionClaw to be co-located).
3. Consider splitting the PR — the bug fix and the BastionClaw adapter are independent and the bundling makes each harder to review.

Issue #3168 Orphaned runs block agent queue: queued runs not cancelled when issue closes + reaper skips zombie processes
ALIGNED low open by @vzert · 2026-04-10T00:29:01Z → gardener comment 1 other
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · type: issue

Aligned with context tree. This issue describes both halves of the orphaned-run problem: queued runs not cancelled when issues close, AND the orphan reaper skipping zombie processes. Three complementary fixes are in flight, and together they address the full failure mode you describe:

- PR #3200 — cancels orphaned queued/running runs when issue is reassigned or closed (event-triggered cleanup)
- PR #3190 — clears stale executionRunId lock metadata when issue leaves in_progress (event-triggered cleanup)
- PR #3218 — SIGTERM→SIGKILL orphaned PIDs in the stale-run reaper, marks them failed (background-triggered cleanup, addresses the "process alive but hung" half)

Gardener flagged all three as NEEDS_REVIEW because they sit close to the [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) "no silent auto-recovery" principle and the boundary between event-triggered cleanup (likely allowed) and background-driven recovery (likely not) is not yet codified in the tree.

### Recommendation

- The three PRs should be coordinated and ideally land together or in a known order to avoid leaving the system in a half-cleaned state.
- Once they land, this issue can be closed.
- Strongest tree-update suggestion in this iteration: product/task-system/NODE.md should add an explicit decision on auto-cleanup vs auto-recovery boundaries. Three orphan-cleanup PRs in one batch is a clear signal the tree is missing a load-bearing decision.

<sub>Reviewed: <code>2026-04-10T00:29:01Z</code> · Tree snapshot: <code>ffda000b</code> · Commands: <code>@gardener re-review</code> · <code>@gardener pause</code> · <code>@gardener ignore</code></sub>

1 other reply (not engaging with gardener)
JaimeBadiola · 2026-04-14T05:04:04Z

Adding a fresh reproduction from production use — this issue just bit us hard and cost several hours of debugging + a blocked pilot launch.

## Repro / timeline

- Agent: CTO (claude_local, sonnet, heartbeat enabled)
- Task: debug a React hooks violation causing production white-page
- Heartbeat run dbf916f3 started 2026-04-14T04:45:15 via manual invoke
- Agent loaded cache, cloned repo, ran eslint, got tool result back at 04:57:44
- Then complete silence — no more stdout, no assistant response, no crash
- Paperclip DB still shows status: running, exitCode: null, finishedAt: null
- Child claude --print process (PID 83234) stayed alive at 0.3% CPU, 190MB RSS, for 70+ minutes before I killed it manually
- Meanwhile the next manually-invoked heartbeat 005657c5 sat in queued — never started — because HEARTBEAT_MAX_CONCURRENT_RUNS_DEFAULT = 1 and the stuck run held the slot.

The reaper ran every 5 min per index.ts:615 with staleThresholdMs: 5 60 1000, but reapOrphanedRuns at heartbeat.ts:2395 skips when processPidAlive === true. There is no max-run-duration cap anywhere in the reaper, so a silent-but-alive child blocks the queue forever.


heartbeat.ts:2421
  if (processPidAlive) {
    // mark as DETACHED_PROCESS_ERROR, continue — never reaps a live PID
    continue;
  }

## Impact

- Agent queue frozen for the duration (here: 70+ min, until human intervention)
- No clear signal to the operator — UI shows "running" indefinitely
- With maxConcurrentRuns: 1, one hung Claude CLI = one agent effectively dead
- Downstream issues blocked (in our case: a critical white-page fix that was already committed locally but the push never ran because the agent session hung)

## What claude --print was stuck on

Last observed tool use: Bash → npx eslint .... Result returned cleanly (is_error: false). After that, silence. Could be:

- A long-poll to the Anthropic API that never returned
- Backpressured stdout if the parent consumer stopped reading
- An un-broken MCP connection

The relevant observation is that Paperclip can't tell the difference and has no watchdog.

## Why PR #3218 mattered

#3218 would have ended this quickly — the stale-run reaper SIGTERM→SIGKILL would have marked dbf916f3 as failed at the 5-min mark and let the queue advance. It was closed unmerged pending the "scheduled auto-recovery vs no-silent-recovery" tree decision. From an operator's perspective:

- This is not silent auto-recovery if the reaper writes a failed status + log entry + error code. That IS surfacing the problem — loudly, at DB level, visible in the UI, with the PID and duration recorded.
- The silent failure is the status quo — a run that stays running forever with no log events, no error, no clock, nothing. That is the actual "hidden auto-recovery" (hiding the fact that the agent is dead).

Suggest the tree node revisit that framing: reaping a 15-min-idle process and marking it failed is closer to "surface the problem" than leaving it as a zombie.

## What we want (prioritised)

1. Max-run-duration cap in reapOrphanedRuns with a sensible default (15 min?) and an env var override. This is the smallest possible fix and would unblock essentially all queue-deadlock reports in this thread.
2. Bonus: expose lastStdoutAt on the heartbeat run so operators can see "running but idle for N min" in the UI, even without changing reaper behavior.
3. Longer term: the lastStdoutAt + a watchdog would let us reap based on inactivity rather than absolute duration, which is probably the better semantic.

Happy to open a fresh PR along the lines of #3218 if the maintainers signal they'd accept it with the failed status + log emission framing. Or to try option 2 first if that's less contentious.

Paperclip commit we hit this on: b649bd4 (tip of main as of ~2 days ago). Workspace: claude_local adapter, standard heartbeat settings.

<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — anti-requirements, control plane vs company
- [product/governance/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/governance/NODE.md) — "Surface problems, don't hide them" / no silent auto-recovery
- [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md) — adapter timeout pattern

### Recommendation

This PR should be split into three before merging, in this order:

1. A separate "core: per-agent circuit breaker for heartbeat failures" PR that explicitly proposes the auto-backoff policy. This is a governance-relevant decision (auto-recovery), needs a tree update before it lands, and absolutely should not ship hidden inside a "tighten social-agent" PR. The 15-minute global heartbeat timeout decision belongs in the same PR.
2. A separate "scripts: truwitz company seed" PR in a examples/ or seeds/ directory if the maintainer is OK with example seeds in the core repo at all. My read of [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) is that this content does not belong in paperclipai/paperclip at all — Paperclip is the control plane, not the company. Truwitz should be its own repo using Paperclip as a dependency, with seed data living there.
3. The actual social-agent calendar throttle (whatever code change the title describes) — but I don't see a corresponding code change in the diff. The 666 LOC are all seeds + instructions + heartbeat policy. Either the calendar throttle is missing or it's hidden inside one of the markdown instruction files. If it's in a .md instruction file, that's a documentation/prompt update, not a code change, and the PR title overstates what it does.

Pulling this apart will let the governance-affecting parts get the review they deserve and keep the core repo from accreting company-specific seeds.

PR #3218 fix(heartbeat): kill orphaned agent processes after server restart
NEEDS_REVIEW medium closed AUTHOR WITHDRAWN by @bartrtl · 2026-04-10T00:27:51Z → gardener comment
(1 comment(s) before gardener on this thread)

🌱 gardener:verdict: NEEDS_REVIEW · severity: medium · commit: e733cee0

> [!CAUTION]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Closes #3215. Adds killOrphanedPid() (SIGTERM → SIGKILL after 5s grace), wires it as a fallback in cancelRunInternal and cancelActiveForAgentInternal when the in-memory ChildProcess handle is gone, and changes the stale-run reaper to actually kill orphaned processes and mark runs failed.

This is the third PR in the queue addressing the orphaned-execution-cleanup pattern (after #3200 cancels orphaned queued runs on reassign/close, and #3190 clears stale executionRunId lock metadata). The trio is internally consistent and complementary, but they should be coordinated.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Reaper kills, doesn't observe | Stale-run reaper now SIGKILLs orphans and marks runs failed | [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) principle 6: "Surface problems, don't hide them. No silent auto-recovery." — but a documented timeout-based reaper is closer to "surfacing a problem as a failure" than to "hiding it" | ❓ Partial |
| SIGTERM-then-SIGKILL grace | 5s grace period before hard kill | Standard process-management pattern | ✅ Aligned |
| Trigger | Reaper runs on a schedule (background); kill is unattended | Tree hasn't drawn the line on whether scheduled cleanup is "auto-recovery" | 🆕 New |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — "Surface problems, don't hide them"
- [engineering/backend/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/engineering/backend/NODE.md) — heartbeat path
- (Suggested new) product/task-system/NODE.md — explicit auto-cleanup boundary

### Recommendation

This is the third PR I've flagged on the same auto-cleanup-vs-auto-recovery question (#3200, #3190, #3218). The boundary needs to be drawn explicitly in the tree before more PRs in this category arrive.

1. Coordinate with #3200 and #3190. All three PRs touch the orphaned-run cleanup path:
- #3200 — cancel queued runs when issue is reassigned/closed (event-triggered)
- #3190 — clear stale executionRunId metadata on issue state transitions (event-triggered)
- #3218 — SIGKILL orphaned PIDs in scheduled reaper (background-triggered)
The first two are gated on explicit human/agent state changes. #3218 is the first one that's purely background-driven — that's a meaningful difference for the "no silent auto-recovery" principle and worth a maintainer decision.
2. The stale-run reaper marking runs failed is a behavior change worth flagging in the changelog. Operators monitoring run status will see failed runs that previously appeared as running-with-warning-log.
3. Add a tree node. product/task-system/NODE.md should codify when scheduled cleanup is allowed vs. forbidden. This category of PR will keep arriving until the tree has an opinion.

Otherwise the implementation is well-scoped and tested.

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · type: issue

Aligned with context tree. This issue documents the well-defined timeoutSec=0 infinite-hang bug in codex_local (and other adapters that default timeoutSec to 0). A candidate fix is in flight: PR #3186 ("fix: apply 30-minute default timeout when timeoutSec is 0") closes this issue by treating timeoutSec <= 0 as "use default 30min" across codex-local, cursor-local, and process adapter execute functions.

The fix surfaces the hang as a timeout instead of an indefinite block, aligning with [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) principle 6 ("Surface problems, don't hide them"). Gardener flagged PR #3186 as NEEDS_REVIEW/low because the same guard is duplicated across 3 adapter packages — see the gardener comment on #3186 for the suggestion to lift the default into adapter-utils.

### Recommendation

- Track PR #3186 as the canonical fix.
- Once #3186 lands (ideally with the adapter-utils lift discussed there), this issue can be closed.
- Consider adding the "default adapter timeout" decision to [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md) so future adapters inherit the rule automatically.

This is a direct alignment win with governance — API key collisions break actor identity, which cascades into mis-routed heartbeats and wrong audit-log attribution.

<details>

PR #3245 fix: strip paperclip payload from agent params
ALIGNED low open PENDING by @jodok · 2026-04-09T22:42:25Z → gardener comment 2 other

🌱 gardener:verdict: ALIGNED · severity: low · commit: 5395100

> [!NOTE]
> Context Review — this checks product-context fit against the project's
> context tree, not code correctness. Run Greptile/CodeRabbit for code review.

### Summary

Hardens the OpenClaw gateway adapter so that agentParams.paperclip is always stripped before sending the gateway agent request, and moves wake context entirely into the message field. Removes the buildStandardPaperclipPayload function and the dead paperclipPayload root-level path. Updates tests to assert wake data is present in the message rather than in the now-removed paperclip root field. Adds a regression test that exercises the legacy payloadTemplate.paperclip strip path. Aligns with adapter architecture and docs-as-contract principles.

<details open>
<summary><strong>Context match</strong></summary>

| Area | Item intent | Tree guidance | Fit |
|------|-------------|---------------|-----|
| Adapter protocol boundary | Strip the paperclip root field that OpenClaw strictly rejects; wake context moves to message text | [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md): "Adapters do NOT define the transcript schema. They parse agent output INTO the shared TranscriptEntry types." Adapters should conform to what external gateways accept, not push internal structs outbound. | ✅ Aligned |
| Gateway adapter pattern | OpenClaw WS protocol requires strict param validation; removing an unknown root field is the correct fix | [adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md): "Transport: WebSocket only. Follows a structured protocol: challenge, connect, agent request, wait, event streaming." | ✅ Aligned |
| Surface problems, don't hide them | Rather than silently passing the paperclip field and hoping OpenClaw ignores it, the fix deletes the field unconditionally so failures surface at the message-contract level | Tree principle: "Surface problems, don't hide them. No silent auto-recovery." | ✅ Aligned |
| Docs sync | README updated to reflect actual outbound contract — wake context in message, no paperclip root field | Tree principle: docs should reflect actual contract, not intended-but-broken state. | ✅ Aligned |
| Regression test coverage | New test pins the strip behavior against persisted payloadTemplate.paperclip fixtures | The previous gardener recommendation was to add exactly this test. PR delivers it. | ✅ Aligned |
| Test update accuracy | heartbeat-comment-wake-batching.test.ts and openclaw-gateway-adapter.test.ts updated to match message-embedded wake data | Accurate test alignment — old assertions checked a field that now doesn't exist; new assertions check the same data in its correct location. | ✅ Aligned |
| Control plane, not execution plane | Removing the paperclipPayload that forwarded internal Paperclip IDs into the gateway request reinforces that Paperclip orchestrates; it doesn't serialize internal state into adapters | [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md): "Control plane, not execution plane. Paperclip never runs agent code directly." | ✅ Aligned |

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Tree nodes referenced</strong></summary>

- [adapters/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/NODE.md) — adapter architecture, local vs gateway pattern, transcript schema ownership
- [adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/adapters/openclaw-gateway/NODE.md) — OpenClaw WS gateway adapter, protocol constraints
- [product/NODE.md](https://github.com/serenakeyitan/paperclip-tree/blob/main/product/NODE.md) — control plane identity, not execution plane

</details>

Looks good to merge once code review clears. The previous recommendation to add a regression test for persisted payloadTemplate.paperclip fixtures has been addressed in this version. No new context concerns.
